</a>\n         feature ID\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         0281485\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR3_10-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GR3-10">\n           [10]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         Website\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.mydelraybeach.com" rel="nofollow">\n          www.mydelraybeach.com\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Delray Beach\n       </b>\n       is a coastal city in\n       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">\n        Palm Beach County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       , United States. As of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Census_2010" title="United States Census 2010">\n        2010 census\n       </a>\n       , the city had a total population of 60,522. The population was estimated at 66,255 in 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCensusEst2015_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USCensusEst2015-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Delray Beach is part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">\n        Miami metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">\n        Early years\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Recorded history began when the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Life_Saving_Service" title="United States Life Saving Service">\n        United States Life Saving Service\n       </a>\n       built the\n       <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Refuge_in_Florida" title="Houses of Refuge in Florida">\n        Orange Grove House of Refuge\n       </a>\n       in 1876. The house derived its name from the grove of mature sour orange and other tropical fruit trees found at the site chosen for the house of refuge, but no record or evidence of who planted the trees has survived.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" </a>\n         </div>\n         The Colony Hotel, built in 1926, was designed by architect\n         <a href="/wiki/Martin_L._Hampton" title="Martin L. Hampton">\n          Martin L. Hampton\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="631" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg/220px-Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg/330px-Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg/440px-Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arcade_Tap_Room.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Arcade Tap Room was a gathering place for Delray\'s\n         <i>\n          Artists and Writer\'s Colony\n         </i>\n         visitors from the mid-1920s to the 1950s.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DBHS_2-6">\n          <a href="#cite_note-DBHS-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Settlement began around 1884, when\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">\n        African-Americans\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">\n        Panhandle of Florida\n       </a>\n       purchased land a little inland from the Orange Grove House of Refuge and began farming. By 1894 the Black community was large enough to establish the first school in the area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1894\n       <a href="/wiki/William_S._Linton" title="William S. Linton">\n        William S. Linton\n       </a>\n       , a Republican US Congressman for\n       <a href="/wiki/Saginaw,_Michigan" title="Saginaw, Michigan">\n        Saginaw, Michigan\n       </a>\n       , bought a tract of land just west of the Orange Grove House of Refuge, and began selling plots in what he hoped would become a farming community. Initially, this community was named after Linton. In 1896\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_Morrison_Flagler" title="Henry Morrison Flagler">\n        Henry Flagler\n       </a>\n       extended his\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_East_Coast_Railway" title="Florida East Coast Railway">\n        Florida East Coast Railroad\n       </a>\n       south from\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">\n        West Palm Beach\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">\n        Miami\n       </a>\n       , with a station at Linton.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Linton settlers began to achieve success, with truck farming of winter vegetables for the northern market. A hard freeze in 1898 was a setback, and many of the settlers left, including William Linton. Partly in an attempt to change the community\'s luck, or to leave behind a bad reputation, the settlement\'s name was changed in 1901 to Delray, after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">\n        Detroit\n       </a>\n       neighborhood of\n       <a href="/wiki/Delray,_Detroit" title="Delray, Detroit">\n        Delray\n       </a>\n       ("Delray" being the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicized" title="Anglicized">\n        anglicized\n       </a>\n       spelling of "Del Rey", which is\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       for "of the king"), which in turn was named after the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" title="Mexican-American War">\n        Mexican-American War\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Molino_del_Rey" title="Battle of Molino del Rey">\n        Battle of Molino del Rey\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Settlers from\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">\n        The Bahamas\n       </a>\n       (then part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">\n        British West Indies\n       </a>\n       ), sometimes referred to as \'Nassaws\', began arriving in the early 1900s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After 1905, newspaper articles and photographs of Delray events reveal that Japanese settlers from the nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Yamato_Colony,_Florida" title="Yamato Colony, Florida">\n        Yamato farming colony\n       </a>\n       also began participating in Delray civic activities such as parades, going to the movies, and shopping. The 1910 census shows Delray as a town of 904 citizens. Twenty-four U.S. states and nine other countries are listed as the birthplace of its residents. Although still a small town, Delray had a remarkably diverse citizenry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DBHS_2-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DBHS-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1911, the area was chartered by the State of Florida as an incorporated town. In the same year,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">\n        pineapple\n       </a>\n       and tomato\n       <a href="/wiki/Canning" title="Canning">\n        canning\n       </a>\n       plants were built. Pineapples became the primary crop of the area. This is reflected in the name of the present day Pineapple Grove neighborhood near downtown Delray Beach.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Prior to 1909, the Delray settlement land was within\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">\n        Dade County\n       </a>\n       . That year,\n       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">\n        Palm Beach County\n       </a>\n       was carved out of the northern portion of the region. In 1915, Palm Beach County and Dade County contributed nearly equal portions of land to create what is now\n       <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">\n        Broward County\n       </a>\n       between the two, leaving Delray situated within the southeastern portion of Palm Beach County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By 1920, Delray\'s population had reached 1,051. In the 1920s, drainage of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Everglades" title="Everglades">\n        Everglades\n       </a>\n       west of Delray lowered the water table, making it harder to grow pineapples, while the extension of the Florida East Coast Railway to\n       <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">\n        Key West\n       </a>\n       resulted in competition from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">\n        Cuban\n       </a>\n       pineapples for the markets of the northern United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_land_boom_of_the_1920s" title="Florida land boom of the 1920s">\n        Florida land boom of the 1920s\n       </a>\n       brought renewed prosperity to Delray. Tourism and real estate speculation became important parts of the local economy. Delray issued\n       <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">\n        bonds\n       </a>\n       to raise money to install water and sewer lines, paved streets, and sidewalks. Several hotels were built. At that time Delray was the largest town on the east coast of Florida between\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">\n        West Palm Beach\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">\n        Fort Lauderdale\n       </a>\n       . The collapse of the land boom in 1926 left Delray saddled with high bond debts, and greatly reduced income from\n       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">\n        property taxes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delray was separated from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       beach by the Florida East Coast Canal (now part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">\n        Intracoastal Waterway\n       </a>\n       ). In 1923 the area between the canal and the ocean was incorporated as Delray Beach. In 1927 Delray and Delray Beach merged into one town named Delray Beach.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F,_Delray_Beach,_FL_(9443786297).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="728" data-file-width="1000" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F%2C_Delray_Beach%2C_FL_%289443786297%29.jpg/220px-Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F%2C_Delray_Beach%2C_FL_%289443786297%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F%2C_Delray_Beach%2C_FL_%289443786297%29.jpg/330px-Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F%2C_Delray_Beach%2C_FL_%289443786297%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F%2C_Delray_Beach%2C_FL_%289443786297%29.jpg/440px-Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F%2C_Delray_Beach%2C_FL_%289443786297%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mrs._Wallace%27s_estate_%3F,_Delray_Beach,_FL_(9443786297).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Estate at 1755 North Ocean Boulevard, January 26, 1933.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Beginning in the mid-1920s, a seasonal\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artists%27_colony" title="Artists\' colony">\n        Artists and Writers Colony\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       was established in Delray Beach and the adjacent town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream,_Florida" title="Gulf Stream, Florida">\n        Gulf Stream\n       </a>\n       . Throughout the 1930s and \'40s, Delray became a winter enclave for artists and authors, especially famous\n       <a href="/wiki/Cartoonist" title="Cartoonist">\n        cartoonists\n       </a>\n       . Two nationally syndicated cartoonists \xe2\x80\x93\n       <a href="/wiki/H._T._Webster" title="H. T. Webster">\n        H. T. Webster\n       </a>\n       (creator of "Caspar Milquetoast") and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fontaine_Fox" title="Fontaine Fox">\n        Fontaine Fox\n       </a>\n       of "Toonerville Trolley" fame \xe2\x80\x93 had offices upstairs in the Arcade Building over the Arcade Tap Room; a gathering place where the artists and writers might be joined by aristocrats, politicians, entertainers, and sports figures. Other well-known artists and writers of the era who had homes in Delray Beach include: Herb Roth, W.J. \xe2\x80\x9cPat\xe2\x80\x9d Enright,\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bernstein_(comics)" title="Robert Bernstein (comics)">\n        Robert Bernstein\n       </a>\n       , Wood Cowan,\n       <a href="/wiki/Denys_Wortman" title="Denys Wortman">\n        Denys Wortman\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Raymond" title="Jim Raymond">\n        Jim Raymond\n       </a>\n       , Charles Williams, Herb Niblick, Hugh McNair Kahler,\n       <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Budington_Kelland" title="Clarence Budington Kelland">\n        Clarence Budington Kelland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nina_Wilcox_Putnam" title="Nina Wilcox Putnam">\n        Nina Wilcox Putnam\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Edna_St._Vincent_Millay" title="Edna St. Vincent Millay">\n        Edna St. Vincent Millay\n       </a>\n       . These seasonal visitors helped soften the effect of the real estate downturn and The Great Depression on the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simon_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Simon-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Depression, not much money was available since the two banks had failed, but progress continued, and the town still looked prosperous because of the previous burst of new buildings during the boom years. The\n       <i>\n        Artists and Writers Colony\n       </i>\n       flourished and Delray Beach\'s fame as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Resort_town" title="Resort town">\n        resort town\n       </a>\n       grew. This era is regarded as Delray Beach\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cgolden age of architecture\xe2\x80\x9d; a period in which the city ranked 50th in population but 10th in building permits in Florida.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prominent architectural styles in Delray Beach from this period include\n       <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">\n        Art Deco\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Revival" title="Mediterranean Revival">\n        Mediterranean Revival\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Revival" title="Mission Revival">\n        Mission Revival\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monterey_Colonial" title="Monterey Colonial">\n        Monterey Colonial\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Streamline_Moderne" title="Streamline Moderne">\n        Streamline Moderne\n       </a>\n       , \'Key West style\' cottages, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bungalows" title="Bungalows">\n        bungalows\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_Districts_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Historic_Districts-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mydelraybeach.com_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mydelraybeach.com-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post_World_War_II">\n        Post World War II\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Post World War II">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seacrest_Hotel.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="688" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Seacrest_Hotel.jpg/220px-Seacrest_Hotel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Seacrest_Hotel.jpg/330px-Seacrest_Hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Seacrest_Hotel.jpg/440px-Seacrest_Hotel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seacrest_Hotel.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Seacrest Hotel.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_Avenue.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="1193" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Atlantic_Avenue.jpg/220px-Atlantic_Avenue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Atlantic_Avenue.jpg/330px-Atlantic_Avenue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Atlantic_Avenue.jpg/440px-Atlantic_Avenue.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_Avenue.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Atlantic Avenue, mid-20th century.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG/220px-Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG/330px-Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG/440px-Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delray_Beach_FL_Marina_Historic_District_12.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Marina_Historic_District" title="Marina Historic District">\n          Marina Historic District\n         </a>\n         , listed in the U.S.\n         <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">\n          National Register of Historic Places\n         </a>\n         , 2014.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For the four years of\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       , citizens of Delray Beach volunteered to watch the beach and ocean 24 hours a day from the faux bell tower atop the seaside Seacrest Hotel. Military personnel patrolled the beach on horseback. Shipping attacks could be seen from the coast. During WWII Delray Beach also saw an influx of service personnel stationed at the nearby\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boca_Raton_Army_Airfield" title="Boca Raton Army Airfield">\n        Boca Raton Army Airfield\n       </a>\n       . Some of the veterans who had trained at the airfield returned to settle in Delray Beach after the war. Steady growth of the city continued though the 1950s and 1960s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DBHS_2-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DBHS-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By the early 1960s Delray Beach was becoming known for\n       <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">\n        surfing\n       </a>\n       . Atlantic Avenue was the biggest seller of surfboards in Florida at the time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Delray Beach\'s surfing fame increased somewhat serendipitously after a 1965 shipwreck. During\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Betsy" title="Hurricane Betsy">\n        Hurricane Betsy\n       </a>\n       , the 441 feet (134\xc2\xa0m) freighter\n       <a href="/wiki/Amaryllis_(ship)" title="Amaryllis (ship)">\n        Amaryllis\n       </a>\n       ran aground on\n       <a href="/wiki/Singer_Island" title="Singer Island">\n        Singer Island\n       </a>\n       , creating a windbreak that formed perfectly breaking waves. The ship was dismantled three years later, yet local\n       <a href="/wiki/Surf_culture" title="Surf culture">\n        surfers\n       </a>\n       have retained an association with the area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1970s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       between Palm Beach Gardens and Miami was fully completed and development began to spread west of the city limits. This pattern continued and accelerated through the 1980s, as downtown and many of the older neighborhoods fell into a period of economic decline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DBHS_2-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DBHS-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Revitalization of some historic areas began during the last decade of the twentieth century, as several local landmark structures were renovated. These include the Colony Hotel\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_School_Square" title="Old School Square">\n        Old School Square\n       </a>\n       (the former campus of Delray Elementary School and Delray High School, since turned into a cultural center).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city also established five\n       <a href="/wiki/Historic_overlay_district" title="Historic overlay district">\n        Historic Districts\n       </a>\n       , listed in the Local Register of Historic Places, and annexed several other historic residential neighborhoods between\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">\n        U.S. Route 1\n       </a>\n       and the Intracoastal Waterway in an effort to preserve some of the distinctive local architecture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_Districts_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Historic_Districts-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mydelraybeach.com_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mydelraybeach.com-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2001, the historic home of teacher/principal Solomon D. Spady was renovated and turned into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spady_Cultural_Heritage_Museum" title="Spady Cultural Heritage Museum">\n        Spady Cultural Heritage Museum\n       </a>\n       . The Spady Museum houses black archives.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-free_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-free-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2007 the museum was expanded by renovating a 1935 cottage as a Kid\'s Cultural Clubhouse, and the construction of a 50-seat amphitheater named for C. Spencer Pompey, a pioneer black educator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Downtown Delray, located in the eastern part of the city, along\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_806" title="Florida State Road 806">\n        Atlantic Avenue\n       </a>\n       , east of I-95 and stretching to the beach, has undergone a large-scale renovation and gentrification. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delray_Beach_Tennis_Center" title="Delray Beach Tennis Center">\n        Delray Beach Tennis Center\n       </a>\n       has brought business to the area. It has hosted several major international tennis events such as the April 2005\n       <a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">\n        Fed Cup\n       </a>\n       (USA vs. Belgium, the April 2004\n       <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">\n        Davis Cup\n       </a>\n       (USA vs. Sweden), the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delray_Beach_International_Tennis_Championships" title="Delray Beach International Tennis Championships">\n        Delray Beach International Tennis Championships\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">\n        ATP\n       </a>\n       Event), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evert" title="Chris Evert">\n        Chris Evert\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">\n        Bank of America\n       </a>\n       Pro Celebrity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoFloCo_1-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SoFloCo-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Community_High_School" title="Atlantic Community High School">\n        Atlantic Community High School\n       </a>\n       was rebuilt in 2005 on a different site from the previous school, a plan which was met with much contention.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When\n       <a href="/wiki/DayJet" title="DayJet">\n        DayJet\n       </a>\n       operated from 2007 to 2008, its headquarters were in Delray Beach.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From 2009 to 2012,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pet_Airways" title="Pet Airways">\n        Pet Airways\n       </a>\n       had its headquarters in Delray Beach.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2012,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rand_McNally" title="Rand McNally">\n        Rand McNally\n       </a>\n       "Best of the Road" named Delray Beach America\'s Most Fun Small Town.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Delray Beach was rated as the 3rd Happiest Seaside Town in America by\n       <i>\n        Coastal Living\n       </i>\n       in 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VolleyballX2.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/VolleyballX2.JPG/220px-VolleyballX2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/VolleyballX2.JPG/330px-VolleyballX2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/VolleyballX2.JPG/440px-VolleyballX2.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VolleyballX2.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Delray Municipal Beach, 2015.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The city\'s eastern boundary includes 3 miles (4.8\xc2\xa0km) of\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beachfront" title="Beachfront">\n         beachfront\n        </a>\n        along the\n        <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n         Atlantic Ocean\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCmap_36-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PBCmap-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Directly to the south, the city is bordered by\n        <a href="/wiki/Boca_Raton,_Florida" title="Boca Raton, Florida">\n         Boca Raton\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCmap_36-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PBCmap-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        To the south and southeast, the city is bordered by\n        <a href="/wiki/Highland_Beach,_Florida" title="Highland Beach, Florida">\n         Highland Beach\n        </a>\n        on the same\n        <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">\n         barrier island\n        </a>\n        east of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">\n         Intracoastal Waterway\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCmap_36-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PBCmap-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Directly to the north, the city is bordered by\n        <a href="/wiki/Boynton_Beach,_Florida" title="Boynton Beach, Florida">\n         Boynton Beach\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCmap_36-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PBCmap-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        To the north and northeast, the city is bordered by\n        <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream,_Florida" title="Gulf Stream, Florida">\n         Gulf Stream\n        </a>\n        on the barrier island and along a section of mainland east of\n        <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">\n         U.S. Route 1\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCmap_36-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PBCmap-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        To the west, an urbanized area that includes\n        <a href="/wiki/High_Point,_Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="High Point, Palm Beach County, Florida">\n         High Point\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Kings_Point,_Florida" title="Kings Point, Florida">\n         Kings Point\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Villages_of_Oriole,_Florida" title="Villages of Oriole, Florida">\n         Villages of Oriole\n        </a>\n        , and multiple\n        <a href="/wiki/Gated_community" title="Gated community">\n         gated communities\n        </a>\n        extends from the city\'s western boundary to the\n        <a href="/wiki/Loxahatchee_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Loxahatchee National Wildlife Refuge">\n         Loxahatchee National Wildlife Refuge\n        </a>\n        portion of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Everglades" title="Everglades">\n         Everglades\n        </a>\n        . Many residences and businesses within this\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suburban" title="Suburban">\n         suburban\n        </a>\n        corridor of unincorporated Palm Beach County possess a Delray Beach postal address despite technically lying outside the\n        <a href="/wiki/City_limits" title="City limits">\n         city limits\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCmap_36-5">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PBCmap-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This area is sometimes referred to collectively and informally as "West Delray."\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n         <a href="#cite_note-37">\n          [37]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Delray Beach\'s location in Southeastern Palm Beach County is in the middle of Florida\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(Florida)" title="Gold Coast (Florida)">\n        Gold Coast\n       </a>\n       region.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the city of Delray Beach has a total land area of 15.81 miles (25.44\xc2\xa0km).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_location">\n        Downtown location\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Downtown location">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In earlier years downtown Delray was centered along Atlantic Avenue as far west as Swinton Avenue and as far east as the intracoastal waterway. Downtown has since expanded. By 2010, downtown extended west to\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">\n        I-95\n       </a>\n       and east as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       ; The north-south boundaries extend roughly two blocks north and south of Atlantic Avenue.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Delray Beach has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">\n        tropical climate\n       </a>\n       , more specifically a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">\n        tropical rainforest climate\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Af\n       </i>\n       ), as its driest month (February) averages 64.8mm of precipitation, meeting the minimum standard of 60mm in the driest month needed to qualify for that designation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delray Beach has hot and humid summers and warm winters, with a marked drier season in the winter. Its near sea-level elevation, coastal location, position just above the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">\n        Tropic of Cancer\n       </a>\n       , and proximity to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">\n        Gulf Stream\n       </a>\n       shapes its climate. Hurricane season officially runs from June 1 through November 30, although hurricanes can develop outside those dates. The most likely time for hurricane activity is during the peak of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde-type_hurricane" title="Cape Verde-type hurricane">\n        Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       season, which is mid-August through the end of September. Delray Beach has received direct or near direct hits from hurricanes in 1903, 1906, 1928, 1947, 1949, 1964, 1965, 1979, 1992, 1999, 2004, and 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height:   </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n     </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2.5%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3.9%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3.6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       As of 2010, there were 34,156 households out of which 20.4% were vacant. As of 2000, 18.9% of households had children under the age of 18 living with them, 42.4% were married couples living together, 10.2% had a female householder with no husband present, and 43.7% were non-families. 35.3% of all households were made up of individuals and 18.3% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.22 and the average family size was 2.87.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2000, the city\'s population was spread out with 18.2% under the age of 18, 6.3% from 18 to 24, 27.1% from 25 to 44, 22.4% from 45 to 64, and 25.9% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 44 years. For every 100 females there were 91.2 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 88.0 males.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2000, the median income for a household in the city was $43,371, and the median income for a family was $51,195. Males had a median income of $33,699 versus $28,469 for females. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">\n        per capita income\n       </a>\n       for the city was $29,350. About 8.2% of families and 11.8% of the population were below the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">\n        poverty line\n       </a>\n       , including 17.6% of those under age 18 and 7.8% of those age 65 or over.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2000, speakers of\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       as a\n       <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">\n        first language\n       </a>\n       accounted for 75.44% of all residents, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">\n        French Creole\n       </a>\n       accounted for 11.73%,\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       consisted of 7.02%,\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       was at 1.87%,\n       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">\n        Italian\n       </a>\n       at 0.88%, and\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       made up 0.75% of the population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2000, Delray Beach had the sixteenth highest percentage of\n       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">\n        Haitian\n       </a>\n       residents in the US, with 10.50% of the population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delray_Beach_Open" title="Delray Beach Open">\n        Delray Beach Open\n       </a>\n       is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">\n        ATP\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_250_series" title="ATP World Tour 250 series">\n        World Tour 250 series\n       </a>\n       men\'s professional\n       <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">\n        tennis\n       </a>\n       tournament held each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delray_Beach_Tennis_Center" title="Delray Beach Tennis Center">\n        Delray Beach Tennis Center\n       </a>\n       has also hosted the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">\n        Fed Cup\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">\n        Davis Cup\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evert" title="Chris Evert">\n        Chris Evert\n       </a>\n       Pro-Celebrity Tennis Classic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Delray Beach Tennis Center is a full-service public tennis facility with 14 clay courts, 6 hard courts, and an 8,200-seat stadium located near downtown on Atlantic Avenue. The center includes an upstairs pavilion and conference room, pro-shop with locker rooms, racquet stringing, and merchandise. The club offers a variety of adult and junior programs, leagues, clinics and camps. A second location, the Delray Swim &amp; Tennis Club, features 24 clay courts and a clubhouse that has a pro shop with merchandise and locker rooms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On July 20, 2010, the city\'s commissioners proclaimed that the city\'s name would be officially changed to Tennis Beach for one week in honor of its nomination by the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Tennis_Association" title="United States Tennis Association">\n        United States Tennis Association\n       </a>\n       as one of the top tennis towns in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_attractions">\n        Culture and attractions\n       </span>\n       <span       The\n         <a href="/wiki/J._B._Evans_House" title="J. B. Evans House">\n          J. B. Evans House\n         </a>\n         , also known as the Sandoway Discovery Center, is listed the U.S. National Register of Historic Places.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delray_Beach_FL_Delray_Beach_Schools01.jpg">\n         <img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Delray_Beach_FL_Delray_Beach_Schools01.jpg/330px-Delray_Beach_FL_Delray_Beach_Schools01.jpg 1.5x, class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delray_Beach_FL_Delray_Beach_Schools01.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Art_Museum_at_Old_School_Square" title="Cornell Art Museum at Old School Square">\n          Cornell Art Museum\n         </a>\n         now occupies part of the restored 1913 Delray School complex.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city has 2 miles (3.2\xc2\xa0km) of public beach accessible from\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_A1A" title="Florida State Road A1A">\n        Florida State Road A1A\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delray_Municipal_Beach_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Delray_Municipal_Beach-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Travel Holiday\n       </i>\n       magazine named Delray Municipal Beach as the top beach in the southeastern United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The remains of the Steamship Inchulva that sank on Sept 11, 1903 are located in shallow water near the public beach, acting as habitat for native fish and corals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Known today as the Delray Wreck, the site is noted for snorkeling and scuba diving.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinkfloridasink.com_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sinkfloridasink.com-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Downtown Delray Beach has undergone a gentrification program centered on East Atlantic Avenue, also known as simply "The Avenue". The area is noted for its nightlife, dining, and shopping.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Atlantic Avenue is also a regular destination for various art fairs and street festivals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delray Beach has a street-legal golf cart community among residents as well as local businesses. Exhilaride offers street-legal golf cart rentals to visitors and residents by the hour, day or longer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Downtowner is point-to-point golf cart free ride service available by app and Katch-a-Ride is a similar business, available by phone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Pineapple Grove Arts District, located downtown just north of Atlantic Avenue, is noted for its galleries, performance art, and cultural organizations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Arts Garage, a not-for-profit multi-media arts venue, hosts musical concerts, live theatre, arts education and outreach programs, and a visual art gallery.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Silverball Museum features more than 150 classic, playable\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinball_machines" title="Pinball machines">\n        pinball machines\n       </a>\n       and arcade games.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Delray Beach Playhouse, which opened in 1947 in Lake Ida East Park, stages plays, musicals, interactive studio theatre, books on stage, children\xe2\x80\x99s theatre productions, classes and camps.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_School_Square" title="Old School Square">\n        Old School Square\n       </a>\n       , the former campus of Delray Elementary School and Delray High School, has since been converted into a cultural center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Old School Square complex now comprises the Crest Theatre, a venue for the performing arts, in the former High School building; the 1925 Gymnasium, restored to maintain its appearance, which has since become a venue for local events such as wedding receptions and dances; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Art_Museum_at_Old_School_Square" title="Cornell Art Museum at Old School Square">\n        Cornell Art Museum\n       </a>\n       , built in the restored Elementary School; and The Pavillion, which serves as an outdoor venue for musical performances and other events such as political rallies. The Creative Arts School offers beginner through master level art, photography, and writing classes for children and adults.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cason Cottage House Museum, once home to a family of Delray Beach pioneers, offers visitors a glimpse at daily life in\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">\n        South Florida\n       </a>\n       from 1915 to 1935. The Museum is maintained and operated by the Delray Beach Historical Society.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Sandoway Discovery Center, located at the historic\n       <a href="/wiki/J._B._Evans_House" title="J. B. Evans House">\n        J. B. Evans House\n       </a>\n       at 142 South\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Road_A1A_(Florida)" title="State Road A1A (Florida)">\n        Ocean Boulevard\n       </a>\n       , features native plants, live animals, and a large collection of shells from around the world. The center offers environmental education programs and classes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The historic\n       <a href="/wiki/John_and_Elizabeth_Shaw_Sundy_House" title="John and Elizabeth Shaw Sundy House">\n        Sundy House\n       </a>\n       now operates as a luxury\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eco_resort" title="Eco resort">\n        eco resort\n       </a>\n       . The premises includes The Sundy family\xe2\x80\x99s former apartments and cottages which have been converted into guest accommodations, a caf\xc3\xa9, an antique shop, and tropical Taru Gardens.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The historic home of teacher/principal Solomon D. Spady was renovated and turned into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spady_Cultural_Heritage_Museum" title="Spady Cultural Heritage Museum">\n        Spady Cultural Heritage Museum\n       </a>\n       . The Spady Museum houses black archives and hosts exhibits and programs designed to recognize the efforts of blacks who were instrumental in shaping Delray Beach and Palm Beach County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-free_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-free-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2007 the museum was expanded by renovating a 1935 cottage as a Kid\'s Cultural Clubhouse, and the construction of a 50-seat amphitheater named for C. Spencer Pompey, a pioneer black educator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Morikami_Museum_and_Japanese_Gardens" title="Morikami Museum and Japanese Gardens">\n        Morikami Museum and Japanese Gardens\n       </a>\n       is a center for\n       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_art" title="Japanese art">\n        Japanese arts\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">\n        culture\n       </a>\n       . The campus includes two museum buildings, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Roji-en_Japanese_Gardens" title="Roji-en Japanese Gardens">\n        Roji-en Japanese Gardens\n       </a>\n       : Garden of the Drops of Dew, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bonsai" title="Bonsai">\n        bonsai\n       </a>\n       garden, library, gift shop, and a Japanese restaurant, called the Cornell Cafe, which has been featured on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Food_Network" title="Food Network">\n        Food Network\n       </a>\n       . Rotating exhibits are displayed in both buildings, and demonstrations, including tea ceremonies and classes, are held in the main building. Traditional Japanese festivals are celebrated several times a year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Wakodahatchee_Wetlands" title="Wakodahatchee Wetlands">\n        Wakodahatchee Wetlands\n       </a>\n       is a wetlands park open to the public. Facilities include a three-quarter mile\n       <a href="/wiki/Boardwalk" title="Boardwalk">\n        boardwalk\n       </a>\n       that crosses between open water pond areas, emergent\n       <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">\n        marsh\n       </a>\n       areas, shallow shelves, and islands with shrubs and snags to foster nesting and roosting. The site is part of the South section of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Florida_Birding_Trail" title="Great Florida Birding Trail">\n        Great Florida Birding Trail\n       </a>\n       and offers many opportunities to observe birds in their natural\n       <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">\n        habitats\n       </a>\n       . Over 151 species of birds have been spotted inside the park, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Pied-billed_grebe" title="Pied-billed grebe">\n        pied-billed grebe\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Snowy_egret" title="Snowy egret">\n        snowy egrets\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Black-bellied_whistling_duck" title="Black-bellied whistling duck">\n        black-bellied whistling ducks\n       </a>\n       . The park is also home to\n       <a href="/wiki/Turtle" title="Turtle">\n        turtles\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alligator" title="Alligator">\n        alligators\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">\n        rabbits\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Frog" title="Frog">\n        frogs\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">\n        raccoons\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The City of Delray Beach maintains five athletic fields, five beach and oceanfront parks, eight community parks, two intracoastal parks, a teen center and\n       <a href="/wiki/Skatepark" title="Skatepark">\n        skatepark\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a splash park,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and a pool and tennis club,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       offering a variety of recreational activities and facilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Delray Beach is one of South Florida\'s most popular beach destinations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The area is noted for its restaurants, retail shops,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nightclubs" title="Nightclubs">\n        nightclubs\n       </a>\n       , art galleries, and hotels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delray_Beach.2C_Florida_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Delray_Beach.2C_Florida-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_development">\n        Recent development\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Recent development">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Downtown Delray Beach has had a building boom since roughly 2003. Recent development reflects trends of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Urbanism" title="New Urbanism">\n        New Urbanism\n       </a>\n       downtown, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mansionization" title="Mansionization">\n        mansionization\n       </a>\n       of waterfront property, sometimes creating pressures on Historic Districts and historic sites.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New\n       <a href="/wiki/Mixed-use_development" title="Mixed-use development">\n        mixed-use development\n       </a>\n       projects have recently been constructed, and more are planned, in the areas immediately north and south of Atlantic Avenue. To accommodate the anticipated growth the city has also built two new municipal parking garages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Drug_recovery_programs">\n        Drug recovery programs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Drug recovery programs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 2007, a\n       <i>\n        New York Times\n       </i>\n       article labeled Delray Beach the drug recovery capital of the United States because it had one of the country\xe2\x80\x99s largest recovery communities and relative number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sober_living_houses" title="Sober living houses">\n        sober living houses\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the lucrative local\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_rehab" title="Drug rehab">\n        drug rehab\n       </a>\n       industry has received mixed reviews from addiction experts and is considered a public nuisance by some residents and city officials.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Persistent complaints of\n       <a href="/wiki/Health_care_fraud" title="Health care fraud">\n        health care fraud\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Insurance_fraud" title="Insurance fraud">\n        insurance fraud\n       </a>\n       , strain on public resources, and a perceived lack of adequate regulation and rehab facility inspections have received media coverage. In July 2017, several national news outlets including the\n       <i>\n        New York Times\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        NBC News\n       </i>\n       published investigative reports detailing fraud allegations within South Florida\'s billion-dollar drug rehab industry, focusing on Delray Beach\'s sober houses. At least 30 arrests for illegal "patient brokering" had been made between July 2016 and July 2017 and more are expected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Top_employers">\n        Top employers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Top employers">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       According to Delray Beach\'s 2014 Comprehensive Annual Financial Report,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the top employers in the city are:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         #\n </td>\n        <td>\n         230\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Opioid_Epidemic">\n        Opioid Epidemic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Opioid Epidemic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Delray Beach has experienced a drastic spike in\n       <a href="/wiki/Opioid" title="Opioid">\n        opioid\n       </a>\n       overdoses in recent years, ascending to a record numbers in 2016 and 2017. The number reached its pinnacle of 96 in October 2016. Most overdoses are a result of\n       <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">\n        Heroin\n       </a>\n       mixed with\n       <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">\n        Fentanyl\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_landmarks_and_buildings">\n        Notable landmarks and buildings\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Beach,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Notable landmarks and buildings">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colony_Hotel_Lobby.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="901" data-file-width="1152" height="172" class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colony_Hotel_Lobby.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Front lobby of the Colony Hotel on East Atlantic Avenue.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delray_Beach_FL_Spady_Museum02.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165"      <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delray_Beach_FL_Spady_Museum02.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The historic home of educator Solomon D. Spady has been converted into the\n         <a href="/wiki/Spady_Cultural_Heritage_Museum" title="Spady Cultural Heritage Museum">\n          Spady Cultural Heritage Museum\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"
